< Rating>
5< /Rating>
< Text>
Poncho's has a nice extensive menu offering excellent Mexican food..both lunch/dinner and breakfast all day. The ingredients are good quality and fresh. Their salsa is made in house and is reason enough to come here and eat. Delicious Carne Asada and fresh, good tacos de pollo among many other items.

Thankfully, Poncho's has gone through some much needed renovation since my last visit: gone are torn, worn booths and some windows with bullet holes..in are decent tables with chairs. The walls have new paint. The place looks cleaner.

The girl who works the counter, brings out food and cleans is friendly, hard working and just plain excellent.

While not a fine dining establishment, if you're looking for good solid Mexican food (and beyond delicious salsa) it's a great place to come. BTW.. Parking is easier in the street than the tiny lot.< /Text>

< Review>
I have been looking for a good Mexican Restaurant since returning to the San Fernando Valley in August. I have not been pleased with any of the places where I shopped over a year ago.
I used to have food from Poncho's delivered. But today I went there in person to get my tacos on National Taco Day. The counter person did not know this and had no clue there was even such a thing!! She claimed the salsa was very hot and spicy, and it was!
I ordered the three hard shell tacos combo. I was very disappointed that ground beef meat was not an option. Neither was shredded beef. So, I had 'steak' tacos. (Carne Asada) The tacos we're just OK, as I had asked for extra tomatoes. Mostly the steak was not too tough, And my dog got the tough, stringy pieces. Rice and beans were acceptable. I will continue my search for the 'perfect' hard shell tacos! I am muched grieved over the loss of Casa de Carlos, where I always had a great taco!!</Review>

<rate>3< /rate><Text>There are pros and cons for this gym. I have a membership for three years for around $9 per month, so it isn't a bad price. This also includes another person coming with me for free every time, and there are no other fees that I need to pay. It was also easy for me to signup and I could pay the entire amount up-front, unlike similarly priced gyms.

Along with the pros above, there are cons: this place tends to lack cleaning supplies, so I've had to begin bringing my own with me every time now. The bathrooms are also filthy, but I've just come to accept that it's a common occurrence at most gyms nowadays--especially in California. Half the time, nobody is at the front desk, so people sneak in a lot. I've seen it happen three times already, and was stunned that they weren't seen. It also can sometimes be extremely hot and stuffy downstairs, so it'd be nice if they invested in some large, industrial fans for the rooms. One last thing that may not matter to others as much as it does to me: this place closes way too early and opens way too late on weekends. I like to get my workouts done throughout the week and the weekends, and I'm usually working late on studies into the night. I wish they opened at 5 A.M. on weekends like they do during the weekdays.</Text>< pics>

<Rate>5< /Rate>< Review>
One of the best old school Italian family style restraunts I've ever been to in the bay. Atmosphere is fun, warm, and cozy, with vintage decor mixed in with classic Italian touches. Plaid tablecloths, crystal candle holders, and hanging grapevines set the mood. Then the friendliest staff brings a basket of warm fresh baked bread, soft and chewy- with butter, or olive oil and balsamic.
There's a large menu with all the classics- calamari, salads, pasta specialties, seafood, pizza. Even a dessert menu, as well as beer and wine. I had the linguine with salmon and shrimp, it did not disappoint, the pasta was great. We also had a pizza, and the chewy crust is on the thinner side with a nice puffy crust on the edge. Sauces are flavorful and fresh tasting, and portions are grand. I have to come back for more. We even walked in to a singer on the accordion on a Sunday eve. Service is very friendly and attentive.< /Review>

< name>
Matthias Sch√∂ner</name>
<Date>1520791036024< /Date><rating>3< /rating>< Review>
Had been there about a year ago, and frankly had no strong recollection, good or bad. So this week we were looking for a nearby Italian Restaurant and decided to try O Sole Mio again. It was a mild disappointment.

The restaurant is spread across two store fronts, making it a bit bigger than it seems when first looking in. There's a quirky charm about it. Slightly over the top. Jukeboxes at every table contrast with Italy-inspired decor. The ambiance is not fabulous, but for a low-key neighborhood restaurant it's cute.

The service is the other positive aspect. They are friendly and attentive.

But the food just wasn't good. My pizza was tasteless. The dough was like cardboard and there was hardly any sauce on it, though strangely the toppings were plentiful. My wife's  eggplant parmigiana was also bland. In retrospect we wished we had cooked at home.

I feel for local businesses that have to absorb ever higher cost for rent and labor, and whose ability to pass these increases on to customers is limited. But to me, an Italian restaurant lives and dies by the quality of its food. And a great, flavorful tomato sauce really does not cost that much to make.< /Review>

Shawn MacDonald<//name>
<date>1311562495508< /date>< rate>
4<//rate>
< Review>
Excellent food and service for a decent price.

Good: food, service, portions
Bad: a little slow, only standard veg Italian options

Service:
Initial drop off of water/bread was inattentive, both for us and for a table next to us. Simply dropped off the items and walked away. The lady at the table next to us wanted to ask a question, but the man dropping off the water just turned his back and walked away. One of the servers had no idea which table was which, and our waitress was shaking her head in amusement as he wandered from table to table trying to deliver a salad to its owner.

Our waitress, however, was quite good. Friendly, attentive, and perhaps extra generous with the wine; 1/2 litre ordered, supposedly 3 glasses worth in it... easily 4+ glasses out of it, though. Didn't catch her name, otherwise I'd toss it up here so people know who to look for.

Food:
My mom ordered prawns with spaghetti and was generally pleased, except for wanted more/bigger prawns. My dad ordered lasagna and, while he was originally wondering why they would include ham inside it, he was also generally pleased. His only complaint was that there was too much cheese; I think specifically too much ricotta inside. I ordered linguini alla marinara and thought it was excellent. Very simple, very tasty. The house pinot grigio was fairly crisp and delightful as well.

My only complaint, and this is a general one with Italian restaurants, is the number of available vegetarian options. This restaurant was a tad worse because there weren't any veg ravioli options; most restaurants I've been to have at least one. I'd really like to see a novel vegetarian Italian option one of these days.

Atmosphere:
Very simple, nice environment; could work for a quiet, romantic night out. Nothing special, but no overly negative characteristics either.< /Review>

< Date>
1418521256052</Date>
< Rating>
5</Rating>
< Text>
You can buy books at the Middlefield Monthly sales or at the Library stores. I especially like the Middlefield Monthly Sales, held on the second Saturday, Sunday and Monday of each month - and books I saw were almost all between 25-50 cents in paper, and $1-3 hardbound . On the first day, Saturday, there is the biggest selection, on the second day. Sunday, prices go down as low as $5 a bag, later in the day. On the third day, Monday, after 6pm, in the Bargain Room, ALL BOOKS ARE FREE, ON MONDAYS ONCE A MONTH - the second Monday of the month in the Bargain Room. There are thousands of books. It's an advantage of living in a well-to-do district - people can afford to make lots of donations, and there are fewer people shopping for them. I found the all-volunteer staff to be wonderfully helpful and friendly. And buying here is for a good cause, it supports the Palo Alto Public Library.< /Text>

This place is awesome, and we had a great experience on our 2 hour visit.  We bowled, each lane has modern computer scoring, and enjoyed their extensive beer  menu (they have a full bar, staffed by an excellent bartender). < Review>
It is with great pleasure that I recommend RIck's Body and Paint to any individual looking for experienced and conscientious staff to handle your automotive repair and paint needs.  I first came to know of Rick's Body and Paint in 2016 when I needed to have the paint redone on my car bumper when my car got sideswiped. I dealt specifically with JR Faquiryan who was always very attentive and responsive to my concerns/questions. I was very satisfied with the paint job in the end.
Unfortunately, in February of this year, I was involved in a 3-car collision and my vehicle suffered extensive front- and back-end damage. I felt comfortable enough to return my vehicle back to Rick's Body and Paint for their help based on my previous experience, and I'm glad that I did so.  JR and the rest of the staff did a great job yet again! JR was great in keeping me updated as much as possible about the repair and I appreciated his frequent contact and back and forth with my insurance company and adjuster.  Although getting my vehicle back took slightly longer than either the staff or myself anticipated, I was willing to wait to ensure my vehicle was just right. My vehicle looked absolutely brand new and ran well! A complete auto detail and promise for a follow-up exterior wax in a few months were also thrown in by JR as further commitment to their great customer service.  The last thing anyone involved in a car accident needs is horrible service for his/her automotive repair.  Thankfully, I experienced absolutely none of that!
Therefore, I would enthusiastically recommend this shop to anyone seeking outstanding and professional staff dedicated to providing their clients with the best customer service and results possible.  You are in good hands with Rick's Body and Paint!<//Review>

< Review>
Rick's Body and Paint in Vaccaville is a 5 star facility due to their customer service and the quality of their repairs. After a hit and run incident I was prospected by a young adult couple in the Walmart parking lot in Rohnert Park asking to fix my car. They told me they were a mobile auto body businesses and after I watched her husband get dents and scratches out of the car I had been trying to get out for years, they told me they had 4 kids. I took their number and told him I would call them about the rest of the work. I also gave them my number and her husband called me relentlessly for weeks telling me he could fix the car for $800 which was much less than my insurance deductible. After about the third phone call I told him I wouldn't let him near my car unless he was going to paint it when he was done fixing it he promised me he would paint the car and repair it for $800 total. I had him come over on a Sunday he was 4 hours late and the sun went down. I asked him not to come to my property, asking how he could repair the car in the dark. He showed up anyways. He brought his wife and father and after they repaired the dents and panel work with Bondo. They told me they needed $100 upfront to go get paint from the auto body shop at this point it was 9:30pm at night and I was skeptical that a paint shop was even open. They came back with grey spray paint from the hardware store and told me it was Primer. They then told me I only have to pay them $600 and I could go to Maaco and have the paint job done for less than $300. I believe them only to discover that Maaco would only paint over the job for another $1000 and I would not have a car for 5 days. This was not an option for me since I am a one-car person and I do not live with my family or have roommates so of course I flipped out. I tried to take it to other shops but everybody told me they would have to dig the workout and not paint over it. The couple blocked my number and refused to take my phone calls. I finally had to turn to JR and Rocky of Rick's Body and Paint to help me access my insurance so I could have rental car coverage while they un did the work. They were friendly and did not judge me because I was conned by obvious drug addicts. I was grateful that they helped me in the pinch and their work was beautiful. I'm so excited to have my car back and feel lucky to have friends in the auto body business. They did not make me feel stupid for being a single women who bought a sob story from losers and not wanting to go through my insurance in the beginning of something that really should have been nipped in the butt. Please remember to take your car to professionals when accidents happen. Do not listen to people who say they can fix your car when they do not work at a shop take it to Rick's you'll be grateful you did!<//Review>

<review>Hopscotch is a tastefully laid out American Japanese fusion food affaire. Small restaurant with seating for maybe 30 inside, a few tables outside.

Our food was pretty stellar. Fried chicken, biscuits and gravy, country potatoes, all great. Drinks were good as well (gin fizz). We did have to wait over 30 minutes for our order to be retaken because our bartender forgot to put it in, so I have to detract a star for that; realistically, I don't see service being an issue at all normally.

Also a great selection of unique scotches which I can't wait to try next time. Be aware the prices are not cheap but the food portions are pretty generous. This place is worth a try, you won't regret it.< /review>< pictures>

Cute little place for some simple but good food. The food portion of the menu is small - 5 or 6 entrees and another 5 or 6 appetizers. The wine selection is quite big and the prices are pretty reasonable. They also have 4 or 5 draft beers to choose from. The food is good quality and done with care and creativity. There is bit of Japanese/Asian influence but overall result is very good. The service is very good. The staff is courteous and attentive without being intrusive. This will be my go-to place if I am in the Oakland area.</review>

I love this kind of upscale Japanese-American fusion food. I haven't seen that much Japanese-American fusion, so I thought that this place was pretty cool and unique. I really enjoyed the food here and the interesting flavors that come from combining Japanese cuisine with American cuisine. I came here for the brunch and got the Braised Pork Belly Benedict. We ordered the uni ravioli, the asparagus, and the fried chicken. <UserId.>111281697089670444391</UserId.><username>Paul Lam</username>< date>
1351954702920<//date>
<rate>4< /rate>< Text>
The staff was attentive, friendly and worked well as a team. I wish the food worked well. Our party was 3 and not one of us gave the food high marks.

The uni in the Yonsei Oysters were undetectable. The oyster and salmon roe overpowered the Uni.

I couldn't taste the tongue in the 1st Base Burger. Luckily it was served cut in half and I picked out the tongue to eat it plain.

Happy hour beer was served in smaller glasses, so not a real happy hour price.

I did enjoy the desserts: Mochi Cake and Butterscotch Pudding.

I had high hopes as the ingredients were intriguing. I probably won't be going back as my try list for the Bay Area is pretty long, but I would give it a try again if someone asked me to go - only because the staff was great and the menu looked great. The food wasn't bad, just didn't the high price.</Text>

<review>A charming quaint local Oakland spot with wonderful food. <Date>1417714536157<//Date><Rate>3</Rate><Text>Hopscotch can be a very conflicting experience.  Brunch is great; dinner is lackluster.  Service is great; then it sucks.  One dish can be amazing; the next dish can be a dud.  I've been here a few times, and always leave scratching my head, wondering how I should feel.  Here are some takeaways:

First of all, the place is TINY.  I think maybe eight tables and a bar with eight stools.  It can be very crowded, so factor that into your plans.

Brunch is very solid.  The fried chicken is out of this world, maybe the best I've had in California.  The Bloody Mary is fantastic.  They'll even do a solid French 75, which isn't always the best experience if the bartender doesn't know their stuff.  If you sit at the bar, the bartenders are always pleasant and your service (and your cocktails) will be great.  Get the donuts, you won't regret it.

A few days ago we went in for a Christmas special "whole lamb platter," which consisted of a few different cuts of lamb, broccoli romanesco, cauliflower puree, and cornbread.  It sounded good in the e-mail, but the dinner was just... underwhelming.  For $65 we got a "portion for two" that was generously made for one, and immediately regretted not ordering something else.  All of the food was fine, but none of it was special.

The service was also pretty bad.  When we asked for cocktail pairings instead of wine pairings, the waitress basically said, "Um, well, the wine is really good. Are you sure you don't want wine?" and then offered no help when it came to cocktails.  In a place that actually has a great bar, you'd think they would be more willing to talk cocktails.  We felt like we were being pushed hard towards the wine pairings in a gross, upselly-type way, and it was a bummer.

I keep thinking I should go back to Hopscotch and give them another try, because for every negative point, there's a positive point.  Really and truly, I've had some great bites and drinks here.  But it's just not solid enough to stay in my thoughts or stomach for long, especially with so many great restaurants in the Oakland/Berkeley area.

Hopscotch needs to up its game.  There are some ballers around here.</Text><pics>None< /pics>< resp>

<review>Came here with a friend for brunch on a Sunday morning around 10:45. Since it was still early, we were seated right away, outside on the patio per our request. Service was wonderful and quick, and they made some nice suggestions for brunch, although their menu is really limited and very much Asian-inspired.

We started our meal with a carafe of Mimosas for $15, which equates to about 1.5 drinks per person. My friend had the kimchi fried rice with miso marinated jidori eggs. We hadn't expected her rice to be so moist and wet, more on the side of risotto than fried rice, though still good. I had the pork belly eggs benedict, which came with a side salad and skillet potatoes. The Benedict was good, though really rich with the creaminess of the egg yolk, hollandaise sauce, and pork belly fat. The side frisee salad had a nice tart vinegrette. The skillet potatoes came out pipping hot on a small cast iron skillet, though it was rather creamy and cheesy, more like potatoes au gratin than the skillet homefries I was expecting for brunch. Since the pork belly eggs benedict was already so rich, the potatoes seemed like excess. I wish I had gotten fruit as a side instead to even the meal out!

Street parking was easy to find. We found out afterwards that their is also a second half to the restaurant two doors down, so there's definitely more seating than the main location shows.< /review>< Rating>
